      <p>There are occasional reports of police beating prisoners. <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a> claims that Dirir Ibrahim Bouraleh died from injuries sustained under torture by Sergeant Major Abdourahman Omar Said from 23 to 27 April 2011. Conditions in the jails are considered worse, with no formal system of care. </p>
      <p>Security forces frequently make illegal arrests.<sup id="cite_ref-FreedomHouse_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FreedomHouse-78">[77]</a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jean-Paul_Noel_Abdi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jean-Paul Noel Abdi (page does not exist)">Jean-Paul Noel Abdi</a>, president of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Djiboutian_League_of_Human_Rights&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Djiboutian League of Human Rights (page does not exist)">Djiboutian League of Human Rights</a>, was arrested on 9 February 2011 after reporting on opposition protests in connection with the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a> earlier that month. According to <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>, he did not support the protests themselves but objected to what he described as <a href="/wiki/Arbitrary_arrest" class="mw-redirect" title="Arbitrary arrest">arbitrary arrests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HRW_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW-79">[78]</a></sup> He was later released on health grounds but the charges remain.<sup id="cite_ref-Amnesty_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amnesty-80">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Choukri_Djibah" title="Choukri Djibah">Choukri Djibah</a> is the Director of Gender for the Ministry of Women and Family, she works with the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> and the government to develop programmes and support for gender justice.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Djibouti_Armed_Forces" title="Djibouti Armed Forces">Djibouti Armed Forces</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Camp_Maryama_during_an_exercise,_Arta_Region,_Djibouti.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Camp_Maryama_during_an_exercise%2C_Arta_Region%2C_Djibouti.jpg/220px-Camp_Maryama_during_an_exercise%2C_Arta_Region%2C_Djibouti.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Camp_Maryama_during_an_exercise%2C_Arta_Region%2C_Djibouti.jpg/330px-Camp_Maryama_during_an_exercise%2C_Arta_Region%2C_Djibouti.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Camp_Maryama_during_an_exercise%2C_Arta_Region%2C_Djibouti.jpg/440px-Camp_Maryama_during_an_exercise%2C_Arta_Region%2C_Djibouti.jpg 2x" data-file-width="862" data-file-height="591"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Camp_Maryama_during_an_exercise,_Arta_Region,_Djibouti.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Maryama base during a martial exercise in the <a href="/wiki/Arta_Region" title="Arta Region">Arta Region</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Djibouti_Armed_Forces" title="Djibouti Armed Forces">Djibouti Armed Forces</a> include the Djibouti National Army, which consists of the Coastal Navy, the Djiboutian Air Force (Force Aerienne Djiboutienne, FAD), and the National Gendarmerie (GN). As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the manpower available for military service was 170,386 males and 221,411 females aged 16 to 49.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> Djibouti <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_military_expenditures" title="List of countries by military expenditures">spent</a> over US$36&nbsp;million annually on its military as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> (141st in the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_International_Peace_Research_Institute" title="Stockholm International Peace Research Institute">SIPRI</a> database). After independence, Djibouti had two regiments commanded by French officers. In the early 2000s, it looked outward for a model of army organization that would best advance defensive capabilities by restructuring forces into smaller, more mobile units instead of traditional divisions. </p>
      <p>The first war which involved the Djiboutian Armed Forces was the <a href="/wiki/Djiboutian_Civil_War" title="Djiboutian Civil War">Djiboutian Civil War</a> between the Djiboutian government, supported by France, and the <a href="/wiki/Front_for_the_Restoration_of_Unity_and_Democracy" title="Front for the Restoration of Unity and Democracy">Front for the Restoration of Unity and Democracy</a> (<i>FRUD</i>). The war lasted from 1991 to 2001, although most of the hostilities ended when the moderate factions of FRUD signed a peace treaty with the government after suffering an extensive military setback when the government forces captured most of the rebel-held territory. A radical group continued to fight the government, but signed its own peace treaty in 2001. The war ended in a government victory, and FRUD became a political party. </p>
      <p>As the headquarters of the IGAD regional body, Djibouti has been an active participant in the Somali peace process, hosting the <a href="/wiki/Arta,_Djibouti" title="Arta, Djibouti">Arta</a> conference in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-Somvir_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Somvir-82">[81]</a></sup> Following the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Government_of_Somalia" title="Federal Government of Somalia">Federal Government of Somalia</a> in 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-Fcacsunesinpshm_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fcacsunesinpshm-83">[82]</a></sup> a Djibouti delegation also attended the inauguration ceremony of Somalia's new president.<sup id="cite_ref-Piuinefs_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Piuinefs-84">[83]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In recent years, Djibouti has improved its training techniques, military command and information structures and has taken steps to becoming more self-reliant in supplying its military to collaborate with the United Nations in peacekeeping missions, or to provide military help to countries that officially ask for it. Now deployed to <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_military_presence">Foreign military presence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Foreign military presence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:11th_MEU_conducts_Sustainment_Training_170105-F-QF982-589.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/11th_MEU_conducts_Sustainment_Training_170105-F-QF982-589.jpg/220px-11th_MEU_conducts_Sustainment_Training_170105-F-QF982-589.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/11th_MEU_conducts_Sustainment_Training_170105-F-QF982-589.jpg/330px-11th_MEU_conducts_Sustainment_Training_170105-F-QF982-589.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/11th_MEU_conducts_Sustainment_Training_170105-F-QF982-589.jpg/440px-11th_MEU_conducts_Sustainment_Training_170105-F-QF982-589.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4547" data-file-height="3026"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:11th_MEU_conducts_Sustainment_Training_170105-F-QF982-589.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Grand_Bara" title="Grand Bara">Grand Bara</a> desert in 2017
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/French_Armed_Forces" title="French Armed Forces">French Forces</a> remained present in Djibouti when the territory gained independence, first as part of a provisional protocol of June 1977 laying down the conditions for the stationing of French forces, constituting a defense agreement. A new defence cooperation treaty between <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and Djibouti was signed in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> on 21 December 2011. It entered into force on 1 May 2014. By that treaty and its security clause, France reaffirmed its commitment to the independence and <a href="/wiki/Territorial_integrity" title="Territorial integrity">territorial integrity</a> of the Republic of Djibouti. As well before independence, in 1962, a <a href="/wiki/French_Foreign_Legion" title="French Foreign Legion">French Foreign Legion</a> unit, the <a href="/wiki/13th_Demi-Brigade_of_the_Foreign_Legion" title="13th Demi-Brigade of the Foreign Legion">13th Demi-Brigade of the Foreign Legion</a> (13 DBLE) was transferred from Algeria to Djibouti to form the core of the French garrison there.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> On 31 July 2011, the (13 DBLE) left Djibouti to the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>. </p>
      <p>Djibouti's strategic location by the <a href="/wiki/Bab-el-Mandeb" title="Bab-el-Mandeb">Bab-el-Mandeb</a> Strait, which separates the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Aden" title="Gulf of Aden">Gulf of Aden</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> and controls the approaches to the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a>, has made it a desirable location for foreign military bases. <a href="/wiki/Camp_Lemonnier" title="Camp Lemonnier">Camp Lemonnier</a> was abandoned by the French and later leased to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Central_Command" title="United States Central Command">United States Central Command</a> in September 2002. The lease was renewed in 2014 for another 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/French_Foreign_Legion" title="French Foreign Legion">French Foreign Legion</a>'s 13 DBLE is still stationed in Djibouti as the largest French military presence abroad, the only one commanded by a <a href="/wiki/Three-star_rank" title="Three-star rank">3-star general</a>. The country also hosts the only overseas <a href="/wiki/Chinese_People%27s_Liberation_Army_Support_Base_in_Djibouti" title="Chinese People's Liberation Army Support Base in Djibouti">Chinese support base</a> and the only overseas <a href="/wiki/Japan_Self-Defense_Force_Base_Djibouti" title="Japan Self-Defense Force Base Djibouti">Japanese military base</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-88">[87]</a></sup> The Italian National Support Military Base is also located in Djibouti.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The hosting of foreign military bases is an important part of Djibouti's economy. The United States pays $63 million a year to rent Camp Lemonnier,<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-88">[87]</a></sup> France and Japan each pay about $30 million a year,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> and China pays $20 million a year.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_88-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-88">[87]</a></sup> The lease payments added up to more than 5% of Djibouti's GDP of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$2.3 billion</span> in 2017. </p>
      <p>China has, in recent times, stepped up its military presence in Africa, with ongoing plans to secure an even greater military presence in Djibouti specifically. China's presence in Djibouti is tied to strategic ports to ensure the security of Chinese assets. Djibouti's strategic location makes the country prime for an increased military presence.<sup id="cite_ref-Nyska_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nyska-91">[90]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_Regions_of_Djibouti.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/The_Regions_of_Djibouti.png/310px-The_Regions_of_Djibouti.png" decoding="async" width="310" height="309" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/The_Regions_of_Djibouti.png/465px-The_Regions_of_Djibouti.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/The_Regions_of_Djibouti.png/620px-The_Regions_of_Djibouti.png 2x" data-file-width="1992" data-file-height="1986"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_Regions_of_Djibouti.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of Djibouti's regions.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Djibouti" title="Districts of Djibouti">Districts of Djibouti</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Djibouti is partitioned into six administrative regions, with <a href="/wiki/Djibouti_(city)" title="Djibouti (city)">Djibouti city</a> representing one of the official regions. It is further subdivided into twenty <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Djibouti" title="Districts of Djibouti">districts</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Djibouti" title="Geography of Djibouti">Geography of Djibouti</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Location_and_habitat">Location and habitat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Location and habitat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:135px;max-width:135px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:151px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Satellite_image_of_Djibouti_in_November_2001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Satellite_image_of_Djibouti_in_November_2001.jpg/133px-Satellite_image_of_Djibouti_in_November_2001.jpg" decoding="async" width="133" height="147" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Satellite_image_of_Djibouti_in_November_2001.jpg/200px-Satellite_image_of_Djibouti_in_November_2001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Satellite_image_of_Djibouti_in_November_2001.jpg/266px-Satellite_image_of_Djibouti_in_November_2001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="744" data-file-height="820"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:153px;max-width:153px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:151px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Satellite_images_of_Djibouti_during_the_night.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Satellite_images_of_Djibouti_during_the_night.png/151px-Satellite_images_of_Djibouti_during_the_night.png" decoding="async" width="151" height="144" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Satellite_images_of_Djibouti_during_the_night.png/227px-Satellite_images_of_Djibouti_during_the_night.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Satellite_images_of_Djibouti_during_the_night.png/302px-Satellite_images_of_Djibouti_during_the_night.png 2x" data-file-width="736" data-file-height="703"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <a href="/wiki/Satellite_imagery" title="Satellite imagery">Satellite images</a> of Djibouti during the day (left) and night (right)
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Djibouti is situated in the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Aden" title="Gulf of Aden">Gulf of Aden</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bab-el-Mandeb" title="Bab-el-Mandeb">Bab-el-Mandeb</a>, at the southern entrance to the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a>. It lies between latitudes 11° and 14°N and longitudes 41° and 44°E, at the northernmost point of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Rift_Valley" title="Great Rift Valley">Great Rift Valley</a>. It is here in Djibouti that the rift between the <a href="/wiki/African_Plate" title="African Plate">African Plate</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Somali_Plate" title="Somali Plate">Somali Plate</a> meet the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Plate" title="Arabian Plate">Arabian Plate</a>, forming a geologic tripoint.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> The tectonic interaction at this tripoint has created the <a href="/wiki/Extreme_points_of_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Extreme points of Africa">lowest elevation of any place in Africa</a> at <a href="/wiki/Lake_Assal_(Djibouti)" title="Lake Assal (Djibouti)">Lake Assal</a>, and indeed, the second lowest depression on dry land found anywhere on earth (surpassed only by the depression along the border of Jordan and Israel). </p>
      <p>The country's coastline stretches 314 kilometres (195 miles), with terrain consisting mainly of plateau, plains and highlands. Djibouti has a total area of 23,200 square kilometres (9,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). Its borders extend 575&nbsp;km (357&nbsp;mi), 125&nbsp;km (78&nbsp;mi) of which are shared with <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a>, 390&nbsp;km (242&nbsp;mi) with <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, and 60&nbsp;km (37&nbsp;mi) with <a href="/wiki/Somaliland" title="Somaliland">Somaliland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> Djibouti is the southernmost <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Plate_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabian Plate country">country on the Arabian Plate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Djibouti has eight mountain ranges with peaks of over 1,000 metres (3,300 feet).<sup id="cite_ref-Hmid_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hmid-94">[93]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mousa_Ali" title="Mousa Ali">Mousa Ali</a> range is considered the country's highest mountain range, with the tallest peak on the border with Ethiopia and Eritrea. It has an elevation of 2,028 metres (6,654 feet).<sup id="cite_ref-Hmid_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hmid-94">[93]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Grand_Bara" title="Grand Bara">Grand Bara</a> desert covers parts of southern Djibouti in the Arta, Ali Sabieh and Dikhil regions. The majority of it sits at a relatively low elevation, below 1,700 feet (520 metres). </p>
      <p>Extreme geographic points include: to the north, Ras Doumera and the point at which the border with Eritrea enters the Red Sea in the Obock Region; to the east, a section of the Red Sea coast north of Ras Bir; to the south, a location on the border with Ethiopia west of the town of <a href="/wiki/As_Ela" class="mw-redirect" title="As Ela">As Ela</a>; and to the west, a location on the frontier with Ethiopia immediately east of the Ethiopian town of <a href="/wiki/Afambo_(woreda)" title="Afambo (woreda)">Afambo</a>. </p>
      <p>Most of Djibouti is part of the <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_xeric_grasslands_and_shrublands" title="Ethiopian xeric grasslands and shrublands">Ethiopian xeric grasslands and shrublands</a> <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a>. The exception is an eastern strip located along the Red Sea coast, which is part of the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_coastal_desert" title="Eritrean coastal desert">Eritrean coastal desert</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Djibouti%27s_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Djibouti%27s_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.png/300px-Djibouti%27s_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="373" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Djibouti%27s_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.png/450px-Djibouti%27s_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Djibouti%27s_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.png/600px-Djibouti%27s_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.png 2x" data-file-width="1824" data-file-height="2268"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Djibouti%27s_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Djibouti map of <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>. <small><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
          <div class="legend">
           <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#FF6700; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">Semi-arid climate</a>
          </div></small> <small>
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
          <div class="legend">
           <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#F10000; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Arid_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Arid climate">Arid climate</a>
          </div></small>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Djibouti's <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> is significantly warmer and has significantly less seasonal variation than the <a href="/wiki/World" title="World">world</a> average. The mean daily maximum <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">temperatures</a> range from 32 to 41&nbsp;°C (90 to 106&nbsp;°F), except at high elevations. In <a href="/wiki/Djibouti_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Djibouti City">Djibouti City</a>, for instance, average afternoon highs range from 28 to 34&nbsp;°C (82 to 93&nbsp;°F) in April. But at <a href="/wiki/Airolaf" title="Airolaf">Airolaf</a>, which ranges from 1,535 to 1,600 m (5,036 to 5,249&nbsp;ft), maximum temperature is 30&nbsp;°C (86&nbsp;°F) in summer and minimum 9&nbsp;°C (48&nbsp;°F) in winter.<sup id="cite_ref-climate_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-climate-96">[95]</a></sup> In the <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/upland" class="extiw" title="wikt:upland">uplands</a> ranges from 500 to 800 m (1,640 to 2,624&nbsp;ft), are comparable and cooler to those on the <a href="/wiki/Coast" title="Coast">coast</a> in the hottest months of June until August. December and January is the coolest month with averages low temperatures falling as low as 15&nbsp;°C (59&nbsp;°F). Djibouti has either a <a href="/wiki/Hot_semi-arid_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot semi-arid climate">hot semi-arid climate</a> (BSh) or a <a href="/wiki/Hot_desert_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot desert climate">hot desert climate</a> (BWh), although <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">temperatures</a> are much moderated at the highest <a href="/wiki/Elevation" title="Elevation">elevations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-climate_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-climate-96">[95]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Djibouti's climate ranges from <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">arid</a> in the northeastern coastal regions to <a href="/wiki/Semiarid" class="mw-redirect" title="Semiarid">semi-arid</a> in the central, northern, western and southern parts of the country. On the eastern seaboard, annual rainfall is less than 5 inches (131&nbsp;mm); in the central highlands, precipitation is about 8 to 16 inches (200 to 400&nbsp;mm). The hinterland is significantly less <a href="/wiki/Humid" class="mw-redirect" title="Humid">humid</a> than the coastal regions. </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Djibouti" title="Wildlife of Djibouti">Wildlife of Djibouti</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:FrancolinusOchropectus.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/FrancolinusOchropectus.svg/220px-FrancolinusOchropectus.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/FrancolinusOchropectus.svg/330px-FrancolinusOchropectus.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/FrancolinusOchropectus.svg/440px-FrancolinusOchropectus.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1052" data-file-height="1052"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:FrancolinusOchropectus.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Djibouti_francolin" class="mw-redirect" title="Djibouti francolin">Djibouti francolin</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Critically_endangered" class="mw-redirect" title="Critically endangered">critically endangered species</a> living only in Djibouti.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The country's <a href="/wiki/Flora" title="Flora">flora</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fauna" title="Fauna">fauna</a> live in a harsh landscape with forest accounting for less than one percent of the total area of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-day_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-day-97">[96]</a></sup> Wildlife is spread over three main regions, namely from the northern mountain region of the country to the volcanic plateaux in its southern and central part and culminating in the coastal region. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Goda_Mountains_-_National_Park_of_For%C3%AAt_du_Day.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Goda_Mountains_-_National_Park_of_For%C3%AAt_du_Day.jpg/220px-Goda_Mountains_-_National_Park_of_For%C3%AAt_du_Day.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Goda_Mountains_-_National_Park_of_For%C3%AAt_du_Day.jpg/330px-Goda_Mountains_-_National_Park_of_For%C3%AAt_du_Day.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Goda_Mountains_-_National_Park_of_For%C3%AAt_du_Day.jpg/440px-Goda_Mountains_-_National_Park_of_For%C3%AAt_du_Day.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="5184"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Goda_Mountains_-_National_Park_of_For%C3%AAt_du_Day.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Plant species on the <a href="/wiki/Day_Forest_National_Park" title="Day Forest National Park">Forêt du Day National Park</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Most species of wildlife are found in the northern part of the country, in the ecosystem of the <a href="/wiki/Day_Forest_National_Park" title="Day Forest National Park">Day Forest National Park</a>. At an average altitude of 1,500 metres (4,921 feet), the area includes the Goda massif, with a peak of 1,783&nbsp;m (5,850&nbsp;ft). It covers an area of 3.5 square kilometres (1&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) of <a href="/wiki/Juniperus_procera" title="Juniperus procera">Juniperus procera</a> forest, with many of the trees rising to 20 metres (66 feet) height. This forest area is the main habitat of the endangered and endemic <a href="/wiki/Djibouti_francolin" class="mw-redirect" title="Djibouti francolin">Djibouti francolin</a> (a bird), and another recently noted vertebrate, <i>Platyceps afarensis</i> (a <a href="/wiki/Colubrine" class="mw-redirect" title="Colubrine">colubrine</a> snake). It also contains many species of woody and herbaceous plants, including boxwood and olive trees, which account for 60% of the total identified species in the country. </p>
      <p>According to the country profile related to biodiversity of wildlife in Djibouti, the nation contains more than 820 species of plants, 493 species of invertebrates, 455 species of fish, 40 species of reptiles, three species of amphibians, 360 species of birds and 66 species of mammals.<sup id="cite_ref-day_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-day-97">[96]</a></sup> Wildlife of Djibouti is also listed as part of <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a> <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot" title="Biodiversity hotspot">biodiversity hotspot</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Aden" title="Gulf of Aden">Gulf of Aden</a> <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reef</a> hotspot.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> Mammals include several species of antelope, such as Soemmerring's gazelle and Pelzeln's gazelle. As a result of the hunting ban imposed since early 1970 these species are well conserved now. Other characteristic mammals are <a href="/wiki/Grevy%27s_zebra" class="mw-redirect" title="Grevy's zebra">Grevy's zebra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamadryas_baboon" title="Hamadryas baboon">hamadryas baboon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hunter%27s_antelope" class="mw-redirect" title="Hunter's antelope">Hunter's antelope</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Warthog" title="Warthog">warthog</a>, a vulnerable species, is also found in the Day National park. The coastal waters have dugongs and <a href="/wiki/Abyssinian_genet" title="Abyssinian genet">Abyssinian genet</a>; the latter needs confirmation by further studies. <a href="/wiki/Green_turtle" class="mw-redirect" title="Green turtle">Green turtles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hawksbill_turtle" class="mw-redirect" title="Hawksbill turtle">hawksbill turtles</a> are in the coastal waters where nestling also takes place.<sup id="cite_ref-Resourcesutviklingshjelp1989_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Resourcesutviklingshjelp1989-99">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-StuartAdams1990_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StuartAdams1990-100">[99]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Northeast_African_cheetah" title="Northeast African cheetah">Northeast African cheetah</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Acinonyx_jubatus_soemmeringii" class="mw-redirect" title="Acinonyx jubatus soemmeringii">Acinonyx jubatus soemmeringii</a></i> is thought to be extinct in Djibouti. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Djibouti" title="Economy of Djibouti">Economy of Djibouti</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:GDP_by_sector,_Djibouti.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/GDP_by_sector%2C_Djibouti.png/250px-GDP_by_sector%2C_Djibouti.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="269" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/GDP_by_sector%2C_Djibouti.png/375px-GDP_by_sector%2C_Djibouti.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/GDP_by_sector%2C_Djibouti.png/500px-GDP_by_sector%2C_Djibouti.png 2x" data-file-width="2881" data-file-height="3099"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:GDP_by_sector,_Djibouti.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Djibouti GDP by sector
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Djibouti's economy is largely concentrated in the service sector. Commercial activities revolve around the country's free trade policies and strategic location as a Red Sea transit point. Due to limited rainfall, vegetables and fruits are the principal production crops, and other food items require importation. The GDP (purchasing power parity) in 2013 was estimated at $2.505&nbsp;billion, with a real growth rate of 5% annually. Per capita income is around $2,874 (PPP). The services sector constituted around 79.7% of the GDP, followed by industry at 17.3%, and agriculture at 3%.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the container terminal at the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Djibouti" title="Port of Djibouti">Port of Djibouti</a> handles the bulk of the nation's trade. About 70% of the seaport's activity consists of imports to and exports from neighboring <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, which depends on the harbour as its main maritime outlet.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> As of 2018, 95% of Ethiopian transit cargo was handled by the Port of Djibouti.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> The port also serves as an international refueling center and transshipment hub.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> In 2012, the Djiboutian government in collaboration with DP World started construction of the <a href="/wiki/Doraleh_Container_Terminal" title="Doraleh Container Terminal">Doraleh Container Terminal</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Cdpafoid_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cdpafoid-103">[102]</a></sup> a third major seaport intended to further develop the national transit capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> A $396&nbsp;million project, it has the capacity to accommodate 1.5&nbsp;million twenty foot container units annually.<sup id="cite_ref-Cdpafoid_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cdpafoid-103">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Djibouti was ranked the 177th safest investment destination in the world in the March 2011 Euromoney Country Risk rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> To improve the environment for direct foreign investment, the Djibouti authorities in conjunction with various non-profit organizations have launched a number of development projects aimed at highlighting the country's commercial potential. The government has also introduced new private sector policies targeting high interest and inflation rates, including relaxing the tax burden on enterprises and allowing exemptions on consumption tax.<sup id="cite_ref-Cdpafoid_103-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cdpafoid-103">[102]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Djibouti.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Tree_map_export_2009_Djibouti.jpeg/250px-Tree_map_export_2009_Djibouti.jpeg" decoding="async" width="250" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Tree_map_export_2009_Djibouti.jpeg/375px-Tree_map_export_2009_Djibouti.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Tree_map_export_2009_Djibouti.jpeg/500px-Tree_map_export_2009_Djibouti.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1103" data-file-height="862"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Djibouti.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A proportional representation of Djibouti's exports.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Additionally, efforts have been made to lower the estimated 60% urban unemployment rate by creating more job opportunities through investment in diversified sectors. Funds have especially gone toward building telecommunications infrastructure and increasing disposable income by supporting small businesses. Owing to its growth potential, the fishing and agro-processing sector, which represents around 15% of GDP, has also enjoyed rising investment since 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Cdpafoid_103-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cdpafoid-103">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>To expand the modest industrial sector, a 56 megawatt geothermal power plant slated to be completed by 2018 is being constructed with the help of <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Global_Environmental_Facility" class="mw-redirect" title="Global Environmental Facility">Global Environmental Facility</a>. The facility is expected to solve the recurring electricity shortages, decrease the nation's reliance on Ethiopia for energy, reduce costly oil imports for diesel-generated electricity, and thereby buttress the GDP and lower debt.<sup id="cite_ref-Cdpafoid_103-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cdpafoid-103">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Djibouti firm Salt Investment (SIS) began a large-scale operation to industrialize the plentiful salt in Djibouti's <a href="/wiki/Lake_Assal_(Djibouti)" title="Lake Assal (Djibouti)">Lake Assal</a> region. Operating at an annual capacity of 4 million tons, the desalination project has lifted export revenues, created more job opportunities, and provided more fresh water for the area's residents.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cdpafoid_103-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cdpafoid-103">[102]</a></sup> In 2012, the Djibouti government also enlisted the services of the China Harbor Engineering Company Ltd for the construction of an ore terminal. Worth $64&nbsp;million, the project enabled Djibouti to export a further 5,000 tons of salt per year to markets in Southeast Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-Xdcssmuatfse_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xdcssmuatfse-105">[104]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Djibouti_GDP_1985_to_2015.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Djibouti_GDP_1985_to_2015.png/300px-Djibouti_GDP_1985_to_2015.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Djibouti_GDP_1985_to_2015.png/450px-Djibouti_GDP_1985_to_2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Djibouti_GDP_1985_to_2015.png/600px-Djibouti_GDP_1985_to_2015.png 2x" data-file-width="915" data-file-height="572"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Djibouti_GDP_1985_to_2015.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Djibouti's gross domestic product expanded by an average of more than 6 percent per year, from US$341&nbsp;million in 1985 to US$1.5&nbsp;billion in 2015.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Djibouti's gross domestic product expanded by an average of more than 6 percent per year, from US$341&nbsp;million in 1985 to US$1.5&nbsp;billion in 2015. The <a href="/wiki/Djiboutian_franc" title="Djiboutian franc">Djiboutian franc</a> is the currency of Djibouti. It is issued by the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Djibouti" title="Central Bank of Djibouti">Central Bank of Djibouti</a>, the country's <a href="/wiki/Monetary_authority" title="Monetary authority">monetary authority</a>. Since the Djiboutian franc is pegged to the U.S. dollar, it is generally stable and inflation is not a problem. This has contributed to the growing interest in investment in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Cdpafoid_103-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cdpafoid-103">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rdbbafi_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rdbbafi-106">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 10 conventional and Islamic banks operate in Djibouti. Most arrived within the past few years, including the Somali money transfer company <a href="/wiki/Dahabshiil" title="Dahabshiil">Dahabshiil</a> and BDCD, a subsidiary of Swiss Financial Investments. The banking system had previously been monopolized by two institutions: the Indo-Suez Bank and the Commercial and Industrial Bank (BCIMR).<sup id="cite_ref-Rdbbafi_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rdbbafi-106">[105]</a></sup> To assure a robust credit and deposit sector, the government requires commercial banks to maintain 30% of shares in the financial institution;<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> a minimum of 300 million Djiboutian francs in up-front capital is mandatory for international banks. Lending has likewise been encouraged by the creation of a guarantee fund, which allows banks to issue loans to eligible small- and medium-sized businesses without first requiring a large deposit or other collateral.<sup id="cite_ref-Cdpafoid_103-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cdpafoid-103">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Saudi investors are also reportedly exploring the possibility of linking the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabian Peninsula</a> via a 28.5-kilometre-long (17.7&nbsp;mi)<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> oversea bridge through Djibouti, referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Bridge_of_the_Horns" title="Bridge of the Horns">Bridge of the Horns</a>. The investor <a href="/wiki/Tarek_bin_Laden" title="Tarek bin Laden">Tarek bin Laden</a> has been linked to the project. However, it was announced in June 2010 that Phase I of the project had been delayed.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">

        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Djibouti" title="Transport in Djibouti">Transport in Djibouti</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_Djibouti%E2%80%93Ambouli_International_Airport.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/The_Djibouti%E2%80%93Ambouli_International_Airport.png/220px-The_Djibouti%E2%80%93Ambouli_International_Airport.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="202" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/The_Djibouti%E2%80%93Ambouli_International_Airport.png/330px-The_Djibouti%E2%80%93Ambouli_International_Airport.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/The_Djibouti%E2%80%93Ambouli_International_Airport.png/440px-The_Djibouti%E2%80%93Ambouli_International_Airport.png 2x" data-file-width="719" data-file-height="659"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_Djibouti%E2%80%93Ambouli_International_Airport.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Main Terminal at <a href="/wiki/Djibouti%E2%80%93Ambouli_International_Airport" title="Djibouti–Ambouli International Airport">Djibouti–Ambouli International Airport</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Djibouti%E2%80%93Ambouli_International_Airport" title="Djibouti–Ambouli International Airport">Djibouti–Ambouli International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Djibouti_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Djibouti City">Djibouti City</a>, the country's only international airport, serves many intercontinental routes with scheduled and chartered flights. <a href="/wiki/Air_Djibouti" title="Air Djibouti">Air Djibouti</a> is the flag carrier of Djibouti and is the country's largest airline. </p>
      <p>The new and electrified <a href="/wiki/Standard_gauge" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard gauge">standard gauge</a> <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa-Djibouti_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Addis Ababa-Djibouti Railway">Addis Ababa-Djibouti Railway</a> started operation in January 2018. Its main purpose is to facilitate freight services between the Ethiopian hinterland and the Djiboutian <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Doraleh" title="Port of Doraleh">Port of Doraleh</a>. </p>
      <p>Car ferries pass the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Tadjoura" title="Gulf of Tadjoura">Gulf of Tadjoura</a> from Djibouti City to <a href="/wiki/Tadjoura" title="Tadjoura">Tadjoura</a>. There is the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Doraleh" title="Port of Doraleh">Port of Doraleh</a> west of Djibouti City, which is the main port of Djibouti. The Port of Doraleh is the terminal of the new Addis Ababa–Djibouti Railway. In addition to the Port of Doraleh, which handles general cargo and oil imports, Djibouti (2018) has three other major ports for the import and export of bulk goods and livestock, the <a href="/wiki/Tadjoura" title="Tadjoura">Port of Tadjourah</a> (potash), the <a href="/wiki/Damerjog" title="Damerjog">Damerjog Port</a> (livestock) and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Port_of_Goubet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Port of Goubet (page does not exist)">Port of Goubet</a> (salt). Almost 95% of Ethiopia's imports and exports move through Djiboutian ports. </p>
      <p>The Djiboutian highway system is named according to the road classification. Roads that are considered primary roads are those that are fully asphalted (throughout their entire length) and in general they carry traffic between all the major towns in Djibouti. </p>
      <p>Djibouti is part of the <a href="/wiki/21st_Century_Maritime_Silk_Road" title="21st Century Maritime Silk Road">21st Century Maritime Silk Road</a> that runs from the Chinese coast to the Upper Adriatic region with its connections to Central and Eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_telecommunications">Media and telecommunications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Media and telecommunications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Djibouti" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Djibouti">Media of Djibouti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Djibouti" title="Telecommunications in Djibouti">Telecommunications in Djibouti</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Djibtelcom2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Djibtelcom2.jpg/220px-Djibtelcom2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Djibtelcom2.jpg/330px-Djibtelcom2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Djibtelcom2.jpg/440px-Djibtelcom2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Djibtelcom2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Djibouti_Telecom" title="Djibouti Telecom">Djibouti Telecom</a> headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Djibouti_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Djibouti City">Djibouti City</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Telecommunications in Djibouti fall under the authority of the Ministry of Communication.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Djibouti_Telecom" title="Djibouti Telecom">Djibouti Telecom</a> is the sole provider of telecommunication services. It mostly utilizes a microwave radio relay network. A fiber-optic cable is installed in the capital, whereas rural areas are connected via wireless local loop radio systems. Mobile cellular coverage is primarily limited to the area in and around Djibouti city. As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 23,000 telephone main lines and 312,000 mobile/cellular lines were in use. The <a href="/wiki/SEA-ME-WE_3_(cable_system)" class="mw-redirect" title="SEA-ME-WE 3 (cable system)">SEA-ME-WE 3</a> <a href="/wiki/Submarine_communications_cable" title="Submarine communications cable">submarine cable</a> operates to <a href="/wiki/Jeddah" title="Jeddah">Jeddah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suez" title="Suez">Suez</a>, Sicily, <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombo" title="Colombo">Colombo</a>, Singapore and beyond. Telephone <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellite</a> earth stations include 1 <a href="/wiki/Intelsat" title="Intelsat">Intelsat</a> (Indian Ocean) and 1 <a href="/wiki/Arabsat" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabsat">Arabsat</a>. Medarabtel is the regional microwave radio relay telephone network.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Radio_Television_of_Djibouti" title="Radio Television of Djibouti">Radio Television of Djibouti</a> is the state-owned national broadcaster. It operates the sole terrestrial TV station, as well as the two domestic radio networks on <a href="/wiki/AM_broadcasting" title="AM broadcasting">AM</a> 1, <a href="/wiki/FM_broadcasting" title="FM broadcasting">FM</a> 2, and shortwave 0. Licensing and operation of broadcast media is regulated by the government.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> Movie theaters include the Odeon Cinema in the capital.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 215 local internet service providers. Internet users comprised around 99,000 individuals (2015). The internet country top-level domain is <a href="/wiki/.dj" title=".dj">.dj</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Djibouti" title="Tourism in Djibouti">Tourism in Djibouti</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Photo_of_Gulf_Of_Tadjoura.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Photo_of_Gulf_Of_Tadjoura.png/220px-Photo_of_Gulf_Of_Tadjoura.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Photo_of_Gulf_Of_Tadjoura.png/330px-Photo_of_Gulf_Of_Tadjoura.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Photo_of_Gulf_Of_Tadjoura.png/440px-Photo_of_Gulf_Of_Tadjoura.png 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="518"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Photo_of_Gulf_Of_Tadjoura.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Arta Plage on the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Tadjoura" title="Gulf of Tadjoura">Gulf of Tadjoura</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Tourism in Djibouti is one of the growing economic sectors of the country and is an industry that generates less than 80,000 arrivals per year, mostly the family and friends of the soldiers stationed in the country's major naval bases.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> Although the numbers are on the rise, there are talks of the visa on arrival being stopped, which could limit tourism growth. </p>
      <p>Infrastructure makes it difficult for tourists to travel independently and costs of private tours are high. Since the re-opening of the train line from Addis Ababa to Djibouti in January 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> travel by land has also resumed. Djibouti's two main geological marvels, Lake Abbe and Lake Assal, are the country's top tourist destinations. The two sites draw<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> hundreds of tourists every year looking for remote places that are not visited by many. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Djibouti" title="Energy in Djibouti">Energy in Djibouti</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Djibouti has an installed electrical power generating capacity of 126 MW from fuel oil and diesel plants.<sup id="cite_ref-oxford_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oxford-120">[119]</a></sup> In 2002 electrical power output was put at 232 GWh, with consumption at 216 GWh. At 2015, per capita annual electricity consumption is about 330 kilowatt-hours (kWh); moreover, about 45% of the population does not have access to electricity,<sup id="cite_ref-oxford_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oxford-120">[119]</a></sup> and the level of unmet demand in the country's power sector is significant. Increased <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a> imports from <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, which satisfies 65% of Djibouti's demand, will play a significant role in boosting the country's renewable energy supply.<sup id="cite_ref-oxford_120-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oxford-120">[119]</a></sup> The geothermal potential has generated particular interest in Japan, with 13 potential sites; they have already started the construction on one site near Lake Assal. The construction of the photovoltaic power station (solar farms) in Grand Bara will generate 50 MW capacity. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Djibouti" title="Demographics of Djibouti">Demographics of Djibouti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Djiboutian" class="mw-redirect" title="Djiboutian">Djiboutian</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:308px;max-width:308px">

      <p>Djibouti has a population of about 921,804 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-122">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-123">[122]</a></sup> It is a <a href="/wiki/Multiethnic" class="mw-redirect" title="Multiethnic">multiethnic</a> country. The local population grew rapidly during the latter half of the 20th century, increasing from about 69,589 in 1955 to around 869,099 by 2015. The two largest ethnic groups native to Djibouti are the <a href="/wiki/Somalis" title="Somalis">Somalis</a> (60%) and the <a href="/wiki/Afar_people" title="Afar people">Afar</a> (35%). The <a href="/wiki/Somali_clan" class="mw-redirect" title="Somali clan">Somali clan</a> component is mainly composed of the <a href="/wiki/Issa_(clan)" title="Issa (clan)">Issa</a> <a href="/wiki/Dir_(clan)" title="Dir (clan)">Dir</a>, followed by a sizable group of <a href="/wiki/Gadabuursi" title="Gadabuursi">Gadabuursi</a> <a href="/wiki/Dir_(clan)" title="Dir (clan)">Dir</a> and a smaller population of <a href="/wiki/Isaaq" title="Isaaq">Isaaq</a>, mainly the subclan <a href="/wiki/Sacad_Muuse" class="mw-redirect" title="Sacad Muuse">Sacad Muuse</a>. The remaining 5% of Djibouti's population primarily consists of <a href="/wiki/Yemenis" class="mw-redirect" title="Yemenis">Yemeni Arabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/People_of_Ethiopia" title="People of Ethiopia">Ethiopians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Europeans" class="mw-redirect" title="Europeans">Europeans</a> (<a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italians</a>). Approximately 76% of local residents are urban dwellers; the remainder are <a href="/wiki/Pastoralism" title="Pastoralism">pastoralists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> Djibouti also hosts a number of immigrants and refugees from neighboring states, with Djibouti City nicknamed the "French Hong Kong in the Red Sea" due to its cosmopolitan urbanism.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> Djibouti's location on the eastern coast of Africa makes it a hub of regional <a href="/wiki/Human_migration" title="Human migration">migration</a>, with Somalis, Yemenis, and Ethiopians traveling through the country en route to the <a href="/wiki/Arab_states_of_the_Persian_Gulf" title="Arab states of the Persian Gulf">Gulf</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">northern Africa</a>. Djibouti has received a massive influx of migrants from <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Djibouti" title="Languages of Djibouti">Languages of Djibouti</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Djibouti is a <a href="/wiki/Multilingual" class="mw-redirect" title="Multilingual">multilingual</a> nation.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> The majority of local residents speak <a href="/wiki/Somali_language" title="Somali language">Somali</a> (524,000 speakers) and <a href="/wiki/Afar_language" title="Afar language">Afar</a> (306,000 speakers) as first languages. These idioms are the <a href="/wiki/Mother_tongue" class="mw-redirect" title="Mother tongue">mother tongues</a> of the Somali and Afar ethnic groups, respectively. Both languages belong to the larger <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages" title="Afroasiatic languages">Afroasiatic</a> <a href="/wiki/Cushitic" class="mw-redirect" title="Cushitic">Cushitic</a> family. There are two official languages in Djibouti: <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px"> 
        <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black"> 
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 524.21835811132px; border-left-color:Red"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Red"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Red"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 307.76835371753px; border-left-color:Green"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Green"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Green"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:58.778525229247px 80.901699437495px 0 0; border-top-color:Blue"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Blue"></div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption"> 
         <p>Languages of Djibouti </p> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Blue; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Somali_language" title="Somali language">Somali</a> (60%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Green; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Afar_language" title="Afar language">Afar</a> (35%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Red; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> (2%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:white; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Other (3%)
         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Arabic is of religious importance. In formal settings, it consists of <a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">Modern Standard Arabic</a>. Colloquially, about 59,000 local residents speak the <a href="/wiki/Ta%27izzi-Adeni_Arabic" class="mw-redirect" title="Ta'izzi-Adeni Arabic">Ta'izzi-Adeni Arabic</a> dialect, also known as <i>Djibouti Arabic</i>. French serves as a statutory national language. It was inherited from the colonial period, and is the primary language of instruction. Around 17,000 Djiboutians speak it as a first language. Immigrant languages include <a href="/wiki/Omani_Arabic" title="Omani Arabic">Omani Arabic</a> (38,900 speakers), <a href="/wiki/Amharic" title="Amharic">Amharic</a> (1,400 speakers), and <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> (1,000 speakers).<sup id="cite_ref-ethnologue.com_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnologue.com-128">[127]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Djibouti" title="Islam in Djibouti">Islam in Djibouti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Djibouti" title="Christianity in Djibouti">Christianity in Djibouti</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Djibouti's population is predominantly <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>. <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> is observed by around 94% of the nation's population (approximately 740,000 as of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Djibouti&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>), whereas the remaining 6% of residents are Christian adherents.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px"> 
        <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black"> 
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:Orange"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 791.58150883059px; border-left-color:DodgerBlue"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 307.76835371753px; border-left-color:Maroon"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Maroon"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Maroon"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 93.906250581749px; border-left-color:Green"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Green"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Green"></div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption"> 
         <p>Islam in Djibouti (Pew)<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> </p> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Green; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Sunnism" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunnism">Sunnism</a> (87%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Maroon; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Non-denominational_Muslim" title="Non-denominational Muslim">Non-denominational Muslims</a> (8%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Other Muslim (3%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Orange; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Shiaism" class="mw-redirect" title="Shiaism">Shiaism</a> (2%)
         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Islam entered the region very early on, as a group of persecuted Muslims had sought refuge across the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a> at the urging of the Islamic prophet <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a>. In 1900, during the early part of the colonial era, there were virtually no Christians in the territories, with only about 100–300 followers coming from the schools and orphanages of the few Catholic missions in the <a href="/wiki/French_Somaliland" title="French Somaliland">French Somaliland</a>. The Constitution of Djibouti names Islam as the sole <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a>, and also provides for the equality of citizens of all faiths (Article 1) and freedom of religious practice (Article 11).<sup id="cite_ref-English_constitution_69-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-English_constitution-69">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-constitution_70-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-70">[69]</a></sup> Most local Muslims adhere to the <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a> denomination, following the <a href="/wiki/Shafi%27i" class="mw-redirect" title="Shafi'i">Shafi'i</a> school. The <a href="/wiki/Non-denominational_Muslim" title="Non-denominational Muslim">non-denominational Muslims</a> largely belong to <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufi</a> orders of varying schools.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Religious_Freedom_Report" class="mw-redirect" title="International Religious Freedom Report">International Religious Freedom Report</a> 2008, while Muslim Djiboutians have the legal right to convert to or marry someone from another faith, converts may encounter negative reactions from their family and clan or from society at large, and they often face pressure to go back to Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Djibouti" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Djibouti">Diocese of Djibouti</a> serves the small local <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholicism">Catholic</a> population, which it estimates numbered around 7,000 individuals in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> </p>
